	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">José</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><caption>José</caption><tbody><tr><th scope="row">Gender</th><td>predominantly masculine</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#ADD8E6">Origin</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Word/name</th><td>Latin: <i>Iosephus</i>, Greek: Ιωσήφ, Hebrew: יוֹסֵף</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#ADD8E6">Other names</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Related names</th><td><a href="/wiki/Joseph_(given_name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph (given name)">Joseph</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Xos%C3%A9">Xosé</a>, <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flavio_Josefo" class="extiw" title="es:Flavio Josefo">Josefo</a>, Josetxu or Josetxo (given name in <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>). Feminine forms: Josefa, Josée.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>José</b> is a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> form of the given name <a href="/wiki/Joseph_(given_name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph (given name)">Joseph</a>. While spelled alike, this name is pronounced differently in each language: in Spanish <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[xoˈse]</a></span>, and in Portuguese <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[ʒuˈzɛ]</a></span> (or <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[ʒoˈzɛ]</a></span>).
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, the name <i>José</i>, pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ʒoˈze]</a></span>, is an old vernacular form of Joseph, which is also in current usage as a given name. José is also commonly used as part of masculine name composites, such as José Manuel, José Maria or Antonio José, and also in female name composites like Maria José or Marie-José. The feminine written form is <i>Josée</i> as in French.
</p><p>In Netherlandic <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> however, <i>José</i> is a feminine given name, and is pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[ˈjoːseː]</a></span>; it may occur as part of name composites like Marie-José or as a feminine first name in its own right; it can also be short for the name <i>Josina</i> and even a Dutch <a href="/wiki/Hypocorism" title="Hypocorism">hypocorism</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> of the name <i>Johanna</i>.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <b>Jose</b> is originally a <a href="/wiki/Romano-British_culture" title="Romano-British culture">Romano-Celtic</a> surname, and people with this family name can usually be found in, or traced to, the <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">English county of Cornwall</a>, where it was especially frequent during the fourteenth century; this surname is pronounced <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span>/</a></span></span>, as in the English names <i><b>Jose</b>ph</i> or <i><b>Jose</b>phine</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> According to another interpretation <i>Jose</i> is cognate with <i>Joyce</i>; <i>Joyce</i> is an English and Irish surname derived from the <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a> personal name <i>Iodoc</i> which was introduced to England by the Normans in the form <i>Josse</i>. In medieval England the name was occasionally borne by women but more commonly by men; the variant surname <i>Jose</i> is local to Devon and Cornwall.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The common spelling of this given name in different languages is a case of interlingual <a href="/wiki/Homograph" title="Homograph">homography</a>. Similar cases occur in <a href="/wiki/English_name" title="English name">English given names</a> (Albert, Bertrand, Christine, Daniel, Eric, Ferdinand) that are not exclusive to the English language, and which can be found namely in French with a different pronunciation under exactly the same spelling.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_pronunciation">Spanish pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Spanish pronunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>English speakers tend to approximate the Spanish pronunciation <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[xoˈse]</a></span> as <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;h&#39; in &#39;hi&#39;">h</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; with a <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[z]</span> rather than with an <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[s]</span> sound. In Castilian Spanish, the initial &#x27e8;J&#x27e9; is similar to the <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> &#x27e8;ch&#x27e9; in the name <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Bach</a> and <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Appendix:_Scottish_Gaelic_pronunciation" class="extiw" title="wikt:Appendix: Scottish Gaelic pronunciation">Scottish Gaelic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> &#x27e8;ch&#x27e9; in <i><a href="/wiki/Loch" title="Loch">loch</a></i>, though Spanish &#x27e8;j&#x27e9; varies <a href="/wiki/Spanish_dialects_and_varieties" title="Spanish dialects and varieties">by dialect</a>.
</p><p>Historically, the modern pronunciation of the name <i>José</i> in Spanish is the result of the <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_Spanish_coronal_fricatives" title="Phonological history of Spanish coronal fricatives">phonological history of Spanish coronal fricatives</a> since the fifteenth century, when it departed from <a href="/wiki/Old_Spanish" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Spanish">Old Spanish</a>. Unlike today’s pronunciation of this name, in Old Spanish the initial &#x27e8;J&#x27e9; was a <a href="/wiki/Voiced_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiced postalveolar fricative">voiced postalveolar fricative</a> (as the sound "<i>je</i>" in French), and the middle &#x27e8;s&#x27e9; stood for a <a href="/wiki/Voiced_apicoalveolar_fricative" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced apicoalveolar fricative">voiced apicoalveolar fricative</a> <a href="/wiki/Voiced_apicoalveolar_fricative" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced apicoalveolar fricative">/z̺/</a> (as in the Castilian pronunciation of the word <i>mismo</i>). The sounds, from a total of seven <a href="/wiki/Sibilant" title="Sibilant">sibilants</a> once shared by medieval <a href="/wiki/Ibero-Romance" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibero-Romance">Ibero-Romance</a> languages, were partly preserved in <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>, and have survived integrally in <a href="/wiki/Mirandese_language" title="Mirandese language">Mirandese</a> and in the dialects of <a href="/wiki/Norte_Region,_Portugal" title="Norte Region, Portugal">northern Portugal</a>.
</p><p>In those regions of north-western Spain where the Galician language is spoken, the name is spelt <i>Xosé</i> and pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[ʃo'se]</a></span>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_pronunciation">Portuguese pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Portuguese pronunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>People with the Portuguese given name <i>José</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[ʒuˈzɛ]</a></span> usually have their name pronounced by English speakers approximately as "<i>joe say</i>", which is frequently heard in news media. Examples of this are for instance former President of the European Commission <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso" title="José Manuel Barroso">José Manuel Barroso</a> and football coach <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="José Mourinho">José Mourinho</a>, whose names are commonly pronounced with some degree of precision by world media <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> by resorting to English sounds (i.e. "<i>Joseph</i>" without the "<i>ph</i>", often sounding like "<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">zhoo-<span style="font-size:90%">ZAY</span></i></a>").<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historically, the conventional Portuguese spelling of the name was <i>Joseph</i>, just as in English, though variants like <i>Jozeph</i> were not uncommon.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/5_October_1910_revolution" title="5 October 1910 revolution">1910 revolution</a>, the Portuguese spelling was modernized. The first <a href="/wiki/Reforms_of_Portuguese_orthography" title="Reforms of Portuguese orthography">Reform of Portuguese orthography of 1911</a> elided the final mute consonants &#x27e8;ph&#x27e9; and &#x27e8;th&#x27e9; from Biblical <a href="/wiki/Anthroponyms" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthroponyms">anthroponyms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toponyms" class="mw-redirect" title="Toponyms">toponyms</a> (e.g. <i>Joseph</i>, <i>Nazareth</i>) and replaced them with the <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">diacritic</a> on the final &#x27e8;é&#x27e9;, indicating the stress vowel (e.g. <i>José</i>, <i>Nazaré</i>). In Portuguese, the pronunciation of vowels varies substantially depending on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_where_Portuguese_is_an_official_language" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries where Portuguese is an official language">country</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_dialects" title="Portuguese dialects">regional dialect</a> or <a href="/wiki/Social_identity_theory" title="Social identity theory">social identity</a> of the speaker: in the case of the &#x27e8;o&#x27e9; ranging from <a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">/u/</a> to <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">/o/</a>; and in the case of &#x27e8;é&#x27e9;, from <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid front unrounded vowel">/e/</a> to <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid front unrounded vowel">/ɛ/</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_phonology" title="Portuguese phonology">Portuguese phonology</a> developed originally from thirteenth-century <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a>, having a <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">number of speakers worldwide</a> that is currently larger than <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>. In Portuguese the pronunciation of the graphemes &#x27e8;J&#x27e9; and &#x27e8;s&#x27e9; is in fact phonetically the same as in French, where the name <i>José</i> also exists and the pronunciation is similar, aside from obvious vowel variation and language-specific intonation.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="French_vernacular_form">French vernacular form</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: French vernacular form">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The French given name <i>José</i>, pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ʒoˈze]</a></span>, is an old vernacular form of the French name <i>Joseph</i>, and is also popular under the feminine form <i>Josée</i>. The masculine form is current as a given name, or as short for Joseph as is the case of French politician <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Bov%C3%A9" title="José Bové">José Bové</a>. The same masculine form is also commonly used as part of feminine name composites, as is the case of French athlete <a href="/wiki/Marie-Jos%C3%A9_P%C3%A9rec" title="Marie-José Pérec">Marie-José Pérec</a>. In turn, the feminine form <i>Josée</i> is only used customarily either as a feminine first name or as part of a feminine name composite, with respective examples in French film director <a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9e_Dayan" class="extiw" title="fr:Josée Dayan">Josée Dayan</a> and Canadian actress <a href="/wiki/Marie-Jos%C3%A9e_Croze" title="Marie-Josée Croze">Marie-Josée Croze</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Jewish_use">Jewish use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Jewish use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A number of prominent Jewish men, including sportsmen, entertainers and historical figures, are known publicly as <i>Joseph</i> or <i>Jose</i>, another form of <i>Yossi</i> (Hebrew: יֹוסִי), and a diminutive of <i>Yosef</i> or <i>Yossef</i> (Hebrew: יוֹסֵף).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Feminine_form">Feminine form</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Feminine form">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Both the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> feminine written forms of the name are <a href="/wiki/Josefa_(given_name)" title="Josefa (given name)">Josefa</a>, pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[xoˈsefa]</a></span> in Spanish, and <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[ʒuˈzɛfɐ]</a></span> in Portuguese. The name <i>José</i> also occurs in feminine name composites (e.g. <i>Maria José</i>, <i>Marie-José</i>).
</p><p><i>Josée</i> is a <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> feminine first name, pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ʒoˈze]</a></span>, relates to the longer feminine form of <i>Joséphine</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ʒo'ze'fin]</a></span>, and may also be coupled with other names in feminine name composites.
</p><p>Similarly, in <a href="/wiki/Flemish" title="Flemish">Flemish</a>, <i>José</i> is a male given name, for which the feminine written form is <i>Josée</i>, with both forms being pronounced <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Dutch_and_Afrikaans" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Help:IPA for Dutch and Afrikaans">[ˈioːˌse]</a>, but the spelling stems originally from neighboring French-speaking influence.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, however, <i>José</i> is pronounced <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Dutch_and_Afrikaans" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Help:IPA for Dutch and Afrikaans">[ˈioʊˌseɪ]</a>, which is a feminine given name in its own right, sometimes also used as short for the feminine name <i>Josina</i>. Examples are Olympic swimmer <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Damen" title="José Damen">José Damen</a> and pop singer <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Hoebee" title="José Hoebee">José Hoebee</a>.
</p><p><i>Jospehine</i> and <i>Joséphine</i> are in use in English-speaking countries, while <i>Josefine</i> is popular in Western Europe.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Diminutives">Diminutives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Diminutives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>One of the common Spanish diminutives of the name is <i>Pepe</i>, which is a repetition of the last syllable of the earlier form <i>Josep</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> (Popular belief attributes the origin of Pepe to the abbreviation of <i>pater putativus</i>, P.P., recalling the role of <a href="/wiki/St_Joseph" class="mw-redirect" title="St Joseph">St Joseph</a> in predominantly Catholic Spanish-speaking countries.) In <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Hispanic America</a>, the diminutives <i>Cheché</i> and <i>Chepe</i> also occur, as in Colombian soccer player <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Eugenio_Hern%C3%A1ndez" class="extiw" title="es:José Eugenio Hernández">José Eugenio ("Cheché") Hernández</a> and Mexican soccer player <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Naranjo" class="extiw" title="es:José Naranjo">José ("Chepe") Naranjo</a>.
</p><p>In Portuguese, the most widely used diminutive form of the name is <i>Zé</i>, and less used forms include <i>Zeca</i>, <i>Zezé</i>, <i>Zezinho</i>, <i>Zuca</i>, and <i>Juca</i>. The augmentative of the diminutive may occur as in <i>Zezão</i>, as well as the diminutive of the diminutive <i>Zequinha</i>, Zezinho,Josesito.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: People">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mononyms">Mononyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mononyms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jose_(actor)" title="Jose (actor)">Jose</a> (Malayalam: ജോസ്), Indian <a href="/wiki/Actor" title="Actor">actor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Malayalam_cinema" title="Malayalam cinema">Malayalam films</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_of_Braganza,_Archbishop_of_Braga" title="José of Braganza, Archbishop of Braga">José of Braganza</a> (Portuguese: Bragança), Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">noble</a> of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Braganza" title="House of Braganza">House of Braganza</a>, illegitimate son of <a href="/wiki/Peter_II_of_Portugal" title="Peter II of Portugal">King Peter II</a> and Francisca Clara da Silva, <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">Archbishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Braga" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Braga">Braga</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jose_the_Galilean" title="Jose the Galilean">Jose the Galilean</a> (Hebrew: יוסי הגלילי, (Yose HaGelili)), 1st-2nd century Jewish <a href="/wiki/Rabbi" title="Rabbi">rabbi</a>, member of the <a href="/wiki/Tannaim" title="Tannaim">Tannaim</a> involved in compiling the <a href="/wiki/Mishna" class="mw-redirect" title="Mishna">Mishna</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9,_Prince_of_Brazil" title="José, Prince of Brazil">Prince José</a>, Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">noble</a> of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Braganza" title="House of Braganza">House of Braganza</a> (Portuguese: Bragança), son of <a href="/wiki/Maria_I_of_Portugal" title="Maria I of Portugal">Queen Maria I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_III_of_Portugal" title="Peter III of Portugal">King Peter III</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heir_apparent" title="Heir apparent">heir apparent</a> with many <a href="/wiki/List_of_titles_and_honours_of_the_Portuguese_Crown" title="List of titles and honours of the Portuguese Crown">titles</a> including Prince of Brazil and Duke of Braganza, died of <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> at age 27 before ascending to the throne</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_I_of_Portugal" title="Joseph I of Portugal">Joseph I of Portugal</a> (José Francisco António Inácio Norberto Agostinho), also known as José I of Portugal</li></ul>

<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Alves_da_Costa" title="José Alves da Costa">José Alves da Costa</a>, Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Corumb%C3%A1" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Corumbá">Corumbá</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Augusto_Alves_Ro%C3%A7adas" title="José Augusto Alves Roçadas">José Augusto Alves Roçadas</a>, military officer and colonial administrator, led troops at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mufilo" title="Battle of Mufilo">Battle of Mufilo</a> in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Portuguese Angola</a> to suppress the <a href="/wiki/Ovambo_people" title="Ovambo people">Ovambo people</a>'s revolt, appointed as <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">governor</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Hu%C3%ADla_Province" title="Huíla Province">District of Hula</a> in Portuguese Angola, then <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Macau" title="Governor of Macau">Governor of Macau</a>, and returned as <a href="/wiki/List_of_colonial_governors_of_Angola" title="List of colonial governors of Angola">Governor General of Angola</a>, commanded troops in Southern <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> against the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(German_Empire)" title="German Army (German Empire)">German army</a>'s <a href="/wiki/German_campaign_in_Angola" title="German campaign in Angola">WWI campaign in Angola</a>, later participated in the <a href="/wiki/28_May_1926_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="28 May 1926 coup d&#39;état">28 May 1926 coup d'état</a> which ended the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_First_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese First Republic">Portuguese First Republic</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Andr%C3%A9s" title="José Andrés">José Ramón Andrés Puerta</a>, Spanish-American <a href="/wiki/Chef" title="Chef">chef</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ruiz_Arenas" title="José Ruiz Arenas">José Ruiz Arenas</a>, Bolivian <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assistant_bishop" title="Assistant bishop">Assistant Bishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Bogotá">Bogotá</a>, then Bishop and later <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">Archbishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Villavicencio" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Villavicencio">Villavicencio</a>, entered the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Curia" title="Roman Curia">Roman Curia</a> and served in the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Commission_for_Latin_America" title="Pontifical Commission for Latin America">Pontifical Commission for Latin America</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Council_for_the_Promotion_of_the_New_Evangelisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontifical Council for the Promotion of the New Evangelisation">Pontifical Council for the Promotion of the New Evangelisation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_the_Evangelization_of_Peoples" title="Congregation for the Evangelization of Peoples">Congregation for the Evangelization of Peoples</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Arguedas" title="José María Arguedas"> José María Arguedas Altamirano</a>, Peruvian <a href="/wiki/Novelist" title="Novelist">novelist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poet" title="Poet">poet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anthropologist" title="Anthropologist">anthropologist</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Arpa" title="José Arpa">José Arpa y Perea</a>, Spanish-born <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painter</a>, worked in Spain, Mexico, and Texas, known for <a href="/wiki/Realism_(arts)" title="Realism (arts)">realist</a> <a href="/wiki/Landscape_painting" title="Landscape painting">landscapes</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Enrique_Arrar%C3%A1s" title="José Enrique Arrarás">José Enrique Arrarás</a>, Puerto Rican <a href="/wiki/Lawyer" title="Lawyer">lawyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lecturer" title="Lecturer">university lecturer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, former member of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Legislative Assembly of Puerto Rico">Legislative Assembly of Puerto Rico</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Arroyo_Delgado" title="José Miguel Arroyo Delgado">José Miguel Arroyo Delgado</a>, known as <i>Joselito</i>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Bullfighter" title="Bullfighter">matador</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gervasio_Artigas" title="José Gervasio Artigas">José Gervasio Artigas</a>, Uruguayan <a href="/wiki/Folk_hero" title="Folk hero">national hero</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Astigarraga_Lizarralde" title="José Luis Astigarraga Lizarralde">José Luis Astigarraga Lizarralde</a>, Peruvian <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, Bishop of the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Vicariate_of_Yurimaguas" title="Apostolic Vicariate of Yurimaguas">Apostolic Vicariate of Yurimaguas</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mill%C3%A1n_Astray" title="José Millán Astray">José Millán Astray</a>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/General_officer" title="General officer">general</a> and founder of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Foreign_Legion" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Foreign Legion">Spanish Foreign Legion</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Avillez" title="José Avillez">José de Avillez Burnay Ereira</a>, award-winning Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Chef" title="Chef">chef</a> and <a href="/wiki/Restaurateur" title="Restaurateur">restaurateur</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">José María Alfredo Aznar López</a>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Reformism" title="Reformism">reformist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, active member of the <a href="/wiki/Falange_Espa%C3%B1ola_Independiente" title="Falange Española Independiente">Falangist Syndicalist Student Front</a> in his youth, President of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People&#39;s Party (Spain)">People's Party</a>, served as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Spain">Prime Minister</a> under <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I_of_Spain" title="Juan Carlos I of Spain">King Juan Carlos I</a></li></ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="C">C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Cabral" title="José María Cabral">José María Cabral y Luna</a>, Dominican <a href="/wiki/General_officer" title="General officer">general</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="President of the Dominican Republic">Supreme Chief of the Dominican Republic</a>, then <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_Dominican_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of the Dominican Republic">President</a>, abolished <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">capital punishment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">banishment</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Josse_van_Clichtove" title="Josse van Clichtove">Josse van Clichtove</a>, known in Latin as <i>Judocus Clichtoveus Neoportuensis</i>, Belgian <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theologian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">Humanist</a>, teacher and author, profuse antagonist of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>, librarian and tutor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Paris" title="University of Paris">Sorbonne</a></li></ul>
</div>

<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gonz%C3%A1lez-Lander" title="José González-Lander">José González-Lander</a>, Venezuelan-born <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">civil engineer</a>, responsible for the planning, design and construction of the <a href="/wiki/Caracas_Metro" title="Caracas Metro">Caracas Metro</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Gonz%C3%A1lez_L%C3%B3pez" title="José Manuel González López">José Manuel González López</a>, known professionally as <i>José</i>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> player and coach</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Ortiz" title="José González Ortiz">José González Ortiz</a>, Puerto Rican <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a> and former <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> of <a href="/wiki/Luquillo" class="mw-redirect" title="Luquillo">Luquillo</a></li>

González-Páramo</a>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bank_officer" title="Bank officer">bank executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adviser" title="Adviser">economic adviser</a> to several major public and private institutions including the <a href="/wiki/Banco_de_Espa%C3%B1a" class="mw-redirect" title="Banco de España">Banco de España</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Emilio_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Vel%C3%A1zquez" title="José Emilio González Velázquez">José Emilio González Velázquez</a>, Puerto Rican <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a> and Senator</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Zum%C3%A1rraga" title="Antonio José González Zumárraga">Antonio José González Zumárraga</a>, Ecuadorian <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Roman_Catholic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal (Roman Catholic)">cardinal</a>, member of the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a> (S.J.), <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_bishop" title="Auxiliary bishop">Auxiliary Bishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Quito" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Quito">Quito</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Machala" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Machala">Machala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coadjutor_bishop" title="Coadjutor bishop">Coadjutor Bishop</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">Archbishop</a> of Quito, made a Cardinal by <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> in 2001</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Grimaldo" title="José de Grimaldo">José de Grimaldo y Gutiérrez de Solórzano</a>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">noble</a> titled 1st Marquess of Grimaldo and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">statesman</a>, served three times as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Spain">Secretary of the Universal Bureau</a> under <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">King Philip V</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Nicomedes_Grossi" title="José Nicomedes Grossi">José Nicomedes Grossi</a>, Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Bom_Jesus_da_Lapa" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Bom Jesus da Lapa">Bom Jesus da Lapa</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Guerrero_de_Arcos_y_Molina" title="José María Guerrero de Arcos y Molina">José María Guerrero de Arcos y Molina</a>, Nicaraguan-born <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Honduras" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of Honduras">Acting Head of State of Honduras</a>, then <a href="/wiki/President_of_Nicaragua" title="President of Nicaragua">Head of State of Nicaragua</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Patricio_Guggiari" title="José Patricio Guggiari"> José Patricio Guggiari Corniglione</a>, Paraguayan <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, 32nd <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Paraguay" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of Paraguay">President of Paraguay</a></li>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="H">H</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: H">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jose_ben_Halafta" title="Jose ben Halafta">Jose ben Halafta</a> (Yose ben Halafta. Hebrew: רבי יוסי בן חלפתא), leading 2nd century CE scholar of <a href="/wiki/Halakha" title="Halakha">halakha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aggadah" title="Aggadah">aggadah</a>, mentioned frequently in the <a href="/wiki/Mishnah" title="Mishnah">Mishnah</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9-Maria_de_Heredia" title="José-Maria de Heredia">José-Maria de Heredia</a>, Cuban-born French <a href="/wiki/Poet" title="Poet">poet</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Gonz%C3%A1lez_de_Hermosillo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="José María González de Hermosillo (page does not exist)">José María González de Hermosillo</a>, hero of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">Mexican War of Independence</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Hern%C3%A1ndez_(writer)" title="José Hernández (writer)">José Hernandez</a>, Argentinian journalist, <a href="/wiki/Poet" title="Poet">poet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, best known as author of the epic poem <i>Martín Fierro</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gregorio_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="José Gregorio Hernández">José Gregorio Hernández</a>, Venezuelan <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a>, noted for treating the poor without charge, since his death has gained popular recognition in Latin America and Spain as a source of <a href="/wiki/Intercession_of_saints" title="Intercession of saints">miraculous healing</a> and is invoked by the name "José Gregoriano", given the title "Venerable" by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a>, now being considered for <a href="/wiki/Beatification" title="Beatification">beatification</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_M._Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="José M. Hernández">José M. Hernández</a>, American <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronaut</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Hern%C3%A1ndez_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="José María Hernández González">José María Hernández González</a>, Mexican <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, Bishop of Chilapa (now known as the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Chilpancingo-Chilapa" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Chilpancingo-Chilapa">Diocese of Chilpancingo-Chilapa</a>), then Bishop of Netzahualcóyotl (now known as the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Valle_de_Chalco" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Valle de Chalco">Diocese of Valle de Chalco</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_de_Herrera" title="José Joaquín de Herrera">José Joaquín de Herrera</a>, Mexican <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_officer" title="General officer">general</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Army" title="Mexican Army">Mexican Army</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a>, three times <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_Mexico" title="List of heads of state of Mexico">President of Mexico</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Hoebee" title="José Hoebee">José Hoebee</a>, Dutch <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop singer</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Maria_de_Sousa_Horta_e_Costa" title="José Maria de Sousa Horta e Costa">José Maria de Sousa Horta e Costa</a>, also known as also known as José Maria de Sousa Horta e Costa (de) Almeida e Vasconcelos,  Portuguese soldier, <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diplomat" title="Diplomat">diplomat</a>, twice <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Macau" title="Governor of Macau">Governor of Macau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Portuguese_India" title="List of governors of Portuguese India">Governor of Portuguese India</a></li></ul>
</div>

<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Infante" title="José Miguel Infante">José Miguel Infante y Rojas</a>, Chilean statesman and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, leader under the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of Chile">junta</a> government</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Insulza" title="José Miguel Insulza">José Miguel Insulza</a>, Chilean <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, 9th Secretary General of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ingenieros" title="José Ingenieros">José Ingenieros</a>, born as Giuseppe Ingegnieri, Argentinian <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmacist" title="Pharmacist">pharmacist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Positivism" title="Positivism">positivist</a> <a href="/wiki/Philosopher" title="Philosopher">philosopher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Essay" title="Essay">essayist</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Iturbi" title="José Iturbi">José Iturbi</a>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conducting" title="Conducting">conductor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harpsichordist" title="Harpsichordist">harpsichordist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pianist" title="Pianist">pianist</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Izuzquiza_Herranz" title="José María Izuzquiza Herranz">José María Izuzquiza Herranz</a>, Spanish-born Peruvian <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, member of the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a> (S.J.), Bishop of the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Vicariate_of_Ja%C3%A9n_in_Peru" title="Apostolic Vicariate of Jaén in Peru">Apostolic Vicariate of Jaén in Peru</a></li></ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="J">J</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: J">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_James" title="José James">José James</a>, American <a href="/wiki/Musician" title="Musician">musician</a>, <a href="/wiki/Composer" title="Composer">composer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bandleader" title="Bandleader">bandleader</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Jes%C3%BAs_(athlete)" title="José de Jesús (athlete)">José de Jesús</a>, Puerto Rican <a href="/wiki/Long-distance_running" title="Long-distance running">long-distance runner</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_de_Jes%C3%BAs" title="José Luis de Jesús">José Luis de Jesús Miranda</a>, Puerto Rican-born American <a href="/wiki/Evangelism" title="Evangelism">evangelist</a> who claimed to be <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesus Christ">Jesus Christ</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Antichrist" title="Antichrist">Antichrist</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Jim%C3%A9nez_Fern%C3%A1ndez" class="mw-redirect" title="José Jiménez Fernández">José Jiménez Fernández</a>, known as <i>Joselito</i>, Spanish child star <a href="/wiki/Singing" title="Singing">singer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Songwriter" title="Songwriter">songwriter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">entrepreneur</a> in adulthood, jailed for <a href="/wiki/Arms_trafficking" title="Arms trafficking">gun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade" title="Illegal drug trade">drug trafficking</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Alfredo_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="José Alfredo Jiménez">José Alfredo Jiménez-Sandoval</a>, Mexican <a href="/wiki/Singing" title="Singing">singer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Songwriter" title="Songwriter">songwriter</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ranchera" title="Ranchera">rancheras</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mariano_Jim%C3%A9nez_Wald" title="José Mariano Jiménez Wald">José Mariano Jiménez Wald</a>, Peruvian <a href="/wiki/Lawyer" title="Lawyer">lawyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jurist" title="Jurist">jurist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, twice <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Peru" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Peru">Prime Minister of Peru</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Jover" title="José María Jover">José María Jover Zamora</a>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Historian" title="Historian">historian</a>, university <a href="/wiki/Professor" title="Professor">professor</a>, influential in the development of Spanish <a href="/wiki/Historiography" title="Historiography">historiography</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Esteve_Juan" title="José Esteve Juan">José Esteve Juan</a>, also known as Giuseppe Esteve Stefano, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Vieste" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Vieste">Vieste</a>, then Bishop of Orihuela (now known as the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Orihuela-Alicante" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Orihuela-Alicante">Diocese of Orihuela-Alicante</a>)</li></ul>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="K">K</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: K">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jose_Kalluvelil&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jose Kalluvelil (page does not exist)">Jose Kalluvelil</a>, Indian-born Canadian Syro-Malabar <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syro-Malabar_Catholic_Apostolic_Exarchate_of_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Syro-Malabar Catholic Apostolic Exarchate of Canada">Apostolic Exarch (Archbishop) of Canada</a></li></ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="L">L</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: L">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Cirarda_Lachiondo" title="José María Cirarda Lachiondo">José María Cirarda Lachiondo</a>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_Bishop" class="mw-redirect" title="Auxiliary Bishop">Auxiliary Bishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Seville" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Seville">Seville</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Santander" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Santander">Santander</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Córdoba">Córdoba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">Archbishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Pamplona_y_Tudela" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Pamplona y Tudela">Pamplona y Tudela</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Lacunza_Maestroju%C3%A1n" title="José Luis Lacunza Maestrojuán">José Luis Lacunza Maestrojuán</a>, Spanish-born Panamanian <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Roman_Catholic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal (Roman Catholic)">cardinal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friar" title="Friar">friar</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Augustinian_Recollects" title="Order of Augustinian Recollects">Order of Augustinian Recollects</a> (O.A.R.), <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_bishop" title="Auxiliary bishop">Auxiliary Bishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Panam%C3%A1" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Panamá">Panama</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Chitr%C3%A9" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Chitré">Chitré</a>, then Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_David" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of David">David</a>, made a Cardinal by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> in 2015, the first Panamanian to be so appointed</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Garc%C3%ADa_Lahiguera" title="José María García Lahiguera">José María García Lahiguera</a>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_Bishop" class="mw-redirect" title="Auxiliary Bishop">Auxiliary Bishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Madrid" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Madrid">Madrid</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Huelva" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Huelva">Huelva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">Archbishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Valencia_in_Spain" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Valencia in Spain">Valencia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beatification" title="Beatification">beatified</a> by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> in 2011</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Larrauri_Lafuente" title="José María Larrauri Lafuente">José María Larrauri Lafuente</a>, Spanish Catholic bishop, first as <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_Bishop" class="mw-redirect" title="Auxiliary Bishop">Auxiliary Bishop</a> of Pamplona (now known as the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Pamplona_y_Tudela" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Pamplona y Tudela">Archdiocese of Pamplona y Tudela</a>, then as Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Vitoria" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Vitoria">Vitoria</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Queipo_de_Llano,_7th_Count_of_Toreno" title="José María Queipo de Llano, 7th Count of Toreno">José María Queipo de Llano y Ruiz de Saravia</a>, known in Spain as <i>Conde de Toreno</i>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">noble</a> under the title 7th Count of Toreno and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">statesman</a>, served as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Spain">Prime Minister</a> under <a href="/wiki/Isabella_II_of_Spain" title="Isabella II of Spain">Queen Isabella II</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_P._Laurel" class="mw-redirect" title="José P. Laurel">José Paciano Laurel y García</a>, Philippine <a href="/wiki/Judge" title="Judge">judge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, first and only president of the brief <a href="/wiki/Second_Philippine_Republic" title="Second Philippine Republic">Second Philippine Republic</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Lebr%C3%BAn_Moratinos" title="José Lebrún Moratinos">José Lebrún Moratinos</a>, Venezuelan <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Roman_Catholic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal (Roman Catholic)">cardinal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_bishop" title="Auxiliary bishop">Auxiliary Bishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Maracaibo" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Maracaibo">Maracaibo</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Maracay" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Maracay">Maracay</a>, Bishop of Valencia en Venezuela (now known as the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Valencia_en_Venezuela" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Valencia en Venezuela">Archdiocese of Valencia in Venezuela</a>), then <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">Archbishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Caracas" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Caracas">Caracas</a>, made a Cardinal by <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> in 1983</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_da_Av%C3%A9-Maria_Leite_da_Costa_e_Silva" title="José da Avé-Maria Leite da Costa e Silva">José da Avé-Maria Leite da Costa e Silva</a>, Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Friar" title="Friar">friar</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Trinitarian_Order" title="Trinitarian Order">Trinitarian Order</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, became rector of <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a>'s Trinitarian college, then appointed as inquirer (inquisitor) for the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Inquisition" title="Portuguese Inquisition">Portuguese Inquisition</a>, appointed as Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Angra" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Angra">Angra</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Garc%C3%ADa_de_Le%C3%B3n_y_Pizarro" title="José García de León y Pizarro">José García de León y Pizarro</a>, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">statesman</a>, served as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Spain">First Secretary of State</a> under <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VI_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VI of Spain">King Ferdinand VI</a></li>
<li>José Leonilson Bezerra Dias, Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Design" title="Design">designer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">sculptor</a>, represented in major international collections<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Lewgoy" title="José Lewgoy">José Lewgoy</a>, Brazilian-born American television, film, and theatre <a href="/wiki/Actor" title="Actor">actor</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Lezama_Lima" title="José Lezama Lima">José Lezama Lima</a>, Cuban <a href="/wiki/Writer" title="Writer">writer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poet" title="Poet">poet</a>, considered one of the most influential figures in <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_literature" title="Latin American literature">Latin American literature</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Maria_Bonifacio_Leyva_(or_Leiva)_Per%C3%A9z&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="José Maria Bonifacio Leyva (or Leiva) Peréz (page does not exist)">José Maria Bonifacio Leyva (or Leiva) Peréz</a>, also known as <a href="/wiki/Cajem%C3%A9" title="Cajemé">Cajemé</a> or Kahe'eme, <a href="/wiki/Yaqui" title="Yaqui">Yaqui Indian</a> leader in the revolution against the Mexican government</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gregorio_Liendo" title="José Gregorio Liendo">José Gregorio Liendo Vera</a>, Chilean <a href="/wiki/Activism" title="Activism">political activist</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Lima" title="José de Lima">José de Lima</a>, Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Itumbiara" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Itumbiara">Itumbiara</a>, then Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Sete_Lagoas" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Sete Lagoas">Sete Lagoas</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Yves_Limantour" title="José Yves Limantour">José Yves Limantour y Márquez</a>, Mexican <a href="/wiki/Investor" title="Investor">financier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_Finance_and_Public_Credit_(Mexico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretariat of Finance and Public Credit (Mexico)">Secretary of Finance</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Lim%C3%B3n" title="José Limón">José Limón</a>, Mexican <a href="/wiki/Modern_dance" title="Modern dance">modern dancer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Choreography" title="Choreography">choreographer</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Linares" title="José María Linares">José María Linares Lizarazu</a>, 16th <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bolivia" title="President of Bolivia">President of Bolivia</a> then self-declared <a href="/wiki/Dictator" title="Dictator">"Dictator for Life"</a> until overthrown and exiled for life</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Linhares" title="José Linhares">José Linhares</a>, Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Lawyer" title="Lawyer">lawyer</a>, 14th <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President of Brazil</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Jorge_Loayza" title="José Jorge Loayza">José Jorge Loayza</a>, Peruvian <a href="/wiki/Lawyer" title="Lawyer">lawyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jurist" title="Jurist">jurist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, three times <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Peru" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Peru">Prime Minister of Peru</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_L%C3%B3pez_Dom%C3%ADnguez" title="José López Domínguez">José López Domínguez</a>, Spanish military to the rank of <a href="/wiki/Colonel" title="Colonel">colonel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politician</a>, served as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Spain">Prime Minister</a> under <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_XIII_of_Spain" title="Alfonso XIII of Spain">King Alfonso XIII</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ivo_Lorscheiter" title="Ivo Lorscheiter">José Ivo Lorscheiter</a>, Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_bishop" title="Auxiliary bishop">Auxiliary Bishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Porto_Alegre" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a>, then Bishop of Santa Maria (now known as the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Santa_Maria" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Santa Maria">Archdiocese of Santa Maria</a>, being a proponent of <a href="/wiki/Liberation_theology" title="Liberation theology">Liberation Theology</a> led him into debate with <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Cardinal Ratzinger</a>, Prefect of the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_the_Doctrine_of_the_Faith" title="Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith">Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Guadalupe_Padilla_Lozano" title="José Guadalupe Padilla Lozano">José Guadalupe Padilla Lozano</a>, Mexican <a href="/wiki/Bishop_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Bishop in the Catholic Church">Catholic bishop</a>, Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Veracruz" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Veracruz">Veracruz</a></li></ul>
